## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear second-order mechanical oscillators. Common physical effects include restoring forces from a potential U(x), damping forces depending on v, and external/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * x (undamped spring-mass, small oscillations)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper)
- Constant bias / gravity offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Coulomb/dry friction (sign damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (sliding friction dominated damping)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent drag / high-speed damping)
- Cubic velocity damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation in structures/materials)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order odd stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force with symmetry)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations, periodic potential)
- Driven oscillator (additive periodic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external sinusoidal drive)
- Driven Duffing (nonlinear + forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/complex response regimes)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations, limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent pumping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (another self-oscillation normal form)
- General Li├®nard form: dv_dt = -f(x) * v - g(x), with f(x)=c0 + c1 * x**2 and g(x)=c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (broad class of nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative mechanical oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x^3), reflecting U(x) being even.
- Potential-driven structure: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), it often implies dv_dt = -dU/dx for some U(x) (energy-conserving core dynamics).
- Damping identification via v terms: linear -c*v implies viscous damping; -c*v*Abs(v) suggests quadratic drag; -c*sign(v) suggests dry friction.
- Self-excitation signature: factors like (c0 - c1*x**2)*v or (c0 - c1*v**2)*v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude (limit-cycle formation).
- Periodic forcing detection: explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additions indicate external drive; multiple frequencies (sum of sines/cosines) suggest multi-tone excitation.
- Parametric resonance cue: time-multiplying stiffness forms like (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicate modulation of a parameter rather than an additive force.
- Nonlinear stiffness cue: presence of x**3, x**5, or sin(c*x) terms indicates amplitude-dependent natural frequency (hardening/softening or geometric nonlinearity).
- Energy dissipation rate clue: damping terms typically satisfy v*dv_dt having a negative contribution on average (e.g., -v^2, -|v|^3), guiding sign/structure choices.
- Equilibrium shift: constant or slowly varying offsets in dv_dt (e.g., +c) imply a displaced equilibrium position rather than changed oscillation shape.

- an \(x\,e^{-|x|}\) term (non-polynomial, involves \(|x|\) inside an exponential)

- no extra terms (no constants, no linear \(x\), no \(v\), no \(v^5\), etc.), unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Observation that immediately constrains everything: **none of the candidates contains any term of the form \(x\exp(-|x|)\)** (or any \(\exp(-|x|)\) dependence at all). Since \(x e^{-|x|}\) is not representable exactly by any finite combination of pure polynomials, sines, logs, or exponentials in *other variables* with constant parameters, any candidate lacking this functional form cannot be made identical to GT for all real \(x\).

Also, GT contains \(\sin(v)\). Many candidates only have polynomial powers of \(v\) (like \(v, v^5\)) or \(\log(c v+1)\) or \(\exp(c v)\), but not \(\sin(v)\). Even if the missing \(x e^{-|x|}\) issue didnŌĆÖt exist, those would still fail.
